                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">آتي</orth>
                  </form>, (T, S M, &amp;c.,) aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَبِيتُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَبَاتُ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتُوتَةٌ</foreign> (Lth, T, S A, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَبِيتٌ</foreign> (Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَبَاتٌ</foreign> (Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَيَاتٌ</foreign>, (K,) has two meanings: in that which more commonly obtains, the action is restricted to the night: (Msb:) it is by night, or in night; not in sleep: (M:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ يَفْعَلُ كَذَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">He did such a thing by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night:</hi> (S, Msb, K:) [or <hi rend="ital">he was in the night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">during the night, doing such a thing:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">spent, the night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a night,</hi> or a <hi rend="ital">part</hi> 
                  <hi rend="ital">thereof,</hi> or, as will be seen below, <hi rend="ital">he entered upon the night, doing such a thing:</hi>] like as one says, <foreign lang="ar">ظَلَّ يَفْعَلُ كَذَا</foreign> as meaning “ he did such a thing by day, ” or “ at day-time: ” (S, Msb;*) IKoot and Es-Sarakustee and IKtt say that it has this meaning, and not “ he slept: ” (Msb:) [F adds,] <foreign lang="ar">وَ لَيْسَ مِنَ النَّوْمِ</foreign>, (K,) which is said to mean, “ and the action is not one of sleep; ” so that when one sleeps by night, or at night, it is not correct to say, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ يَنَامُ</foreign>: or, accord. to some, “ its meaning is not that of sleeping; ” so that one may say, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ زَيْدٌ نَائِمًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Zeyd was in the night,</hi> &amp;c., or <hi rend="ital">passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">spent, the night,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">sleeping</hi>]: (MF:) [Fei says,] it is only when one remains awake in the night: and hence the saying in the Kur [xxv. 65], <foreign lang="ar">وَٱلَّذِينَ يَبِيتُونَ لِرَّبِهِمْ سُجَّدًا وَقِيامًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And those who pass the night prostrating themselves to their Lord and standing up</hi> in prayer]: (Msb:) Fr says that <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ الرَّجُلُ</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">The man remained awake all the night,</hi> engaged in acts of obedience or of disobedience: (T, Msb:) [or it means <hi rend="ital">the man entered upon the night;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he was in the night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">during the night,</hi> in any state, or engaged in any action; for] Zj says, (M,) <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ</foreign> is said of any one whom the night has overtaken, (M, K, *) whether he have slept or not slept: (M:) and Lth says, <foreign lang="ar">البَيْتُوتَةُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">the entering upon the night:</hi> one says, <foreign lang="ar">بِتُّ أَصْنَعُ كَذَا وَ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I entered upon the night doing such and such things</hi>]: and he adds, (T,) he who says <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">he slept</hi> commits an error; for you say, <foreign lang="ar">بِتُّ أُرَاعِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النُّجُومَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I entered upon,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">passed, the night</hi>] <hi rend="ital">looking at the stars:</hi> and how can he be sleeping who is looking at them? (T, Msb:) but Mullà 'Abd-El-Hakeem, in his Commentaries on the Mutowwal, says that <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ</foreign> sometimes means <hi rend="ital">he remained, continued, stayed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dwelt,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he alighted and abode, by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night,</hi> whether he slept or not: (MF:) and Ibn-Keysán says that it may be used in the same manner as <foreign lang="ar">نَامَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he slept</hi>]; and also, [as will be explained below,] in the same manner as <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ</foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتُوتَةً صَالِحَةً</foreign> (T) or <foreign lang="ar">طَيِّبَةً</foreign> (A) [<hi rend="ital">He passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">entered upon, the night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a night, in a good manner</hi>]. And <foreign lang="ar">بِتُّ القَوْمَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِتُّ بِهِمْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بِتُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَهُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">entered upon, the night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a night, with,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at the abode of, the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">company of men:</hi> the last of these phrases is the most common]. (A 'Obeyd, M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Secondly, it is used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He became</hi>]; (Msb;) or in the same manner as <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he was</hi>]. (Ibn-Keysán, TA.) One says, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ بِمَوْضِعِ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He became</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">was</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in such a place;</hi> whether in night-time or in day-time. (Msb.) And hence the saying of the lawyers, <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ عِنْدَ ٱمْرَأَتِهِ لَيْلَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He became</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">was</hi>] <hi rend="ital">with his wife one night;</hi> [which is the same as <hi rend="ital">he passed a night</hi> &amp;c.; though this, it will be observed, is not in this instance the signification of the verb alone;] whether sleeping or not. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [Thus it is used both as a “ complete, ” i. e. an attributive, verb, and also as an “ incomplete, ” i. e. a non-attributive, verb.]          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَاتَ</foreign>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَبِيتُ</foreign>, (T, A,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتٌ</foreign>, (T, M, K,) also signifies <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He married,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">took a wife:</hi> (T, A:) [see <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتٌ</foreign> below:] or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he gave in marriage;</hi> syn. of the inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَزْوِيجٌ</foreign>. (Kr, M, K.)    </entryFree>26:T1894,<entryFree id="n3599" key="بيّت البَيْتَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بيّت البَيْتَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بيت البيت</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He constructed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">built, the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْت</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">tent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">house,</hi> &amp;c.]. (M.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بيّت الأَمْرِ</foreign>, [inf. n. as below,] <hi rend="ital">He did,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">performed, the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair, by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night:</hi> (M:) and <hi rend="ital">he thought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">meditated, upon it, considering its end,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">issue,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">result,</hi> (Zj, T, S, M, A, Msb, K,) or <hi rend="ital">entered into it,</hi> (Zj, T,) <hi rend="ital">by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night.</hi> (Zj, T, S, M, &amp;c.) And one says, <foreign lang="ar">بُيِّتَ بِلَيْلٍ</foreign>, (T, A,) meaning the same as <foreign lang="ar">دُبِّرَ بِلَيْلِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It was thought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">meditated, upon,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at night</hi>]: (T:) [for] <foreign lang="ar">بُيِّتَ الشَّىْءُ</foreign> also signifies [simply] <hi rend="ital">the thing was thought upon, and considered as to its end, issue,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">result;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">قُدِّرَ</foreign>. (S.) Accord. to El-Marzookee, they say of a thing that is not done deliberately, and with good consideration of its issue or result, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَمْرٌ قُدِّرَ بِلَيْلٍ</foreign>; [in the text from which this is taken, without the syll. signs;] and hence the saying in the Kur [iv. 83], <foreign lang="ar">بَيَّتَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">طَائِفَةٌ مِنْهُمْ غَيْرِ ٱلَّذِى تَقُولُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A part of them meditateth by night upon doing otherwise than that which thou sayest;</hi> as is indicated in the M, where this is cited; and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">يُبَيِّتُونَ</foreign>, in the continuation of the same passage of the Kur, is explained in the T as meaning <foreign lang="ar">يُدَبِّرُونَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">يُقَدِّرُونَ</foreign>, (i. e. <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ السُّوْءِ</foreign>,) <foreign lang="ar">لَيْلًا</foreign>]: but Aboo-Hilál says that a thing is meditated upon in the night in order that one may apply himself to it with strong purpose, and not be diverted by other things, so that it may be done with more firmness; and he cites the same passage of the Kur. (Ham p. 130.) And hence, in the Kur [iv. 108], <foreign lang="ar">إِذْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">يُبَيِّتُونَ مَا لَا يَرْضَى مِنَ القَوْلِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">When they meditate,</hi> &amp;c., (S, M, Bd, Jel,) <hi rend="ital">by night,</hi> (S, M,) [<hi rend="ital">what He will not approve, of speech,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">and prepare it</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in their minds</hi>] (<foreign lang="ar">يُزَوِّرُونَهُ</foreign> [see art. <foreign lang="ar">زور</foreign>]).                   <hi rend="ital">There is no fasting to him</hi> [meaning <hi rend="ital">his fasting is null</hi>] <hi rend="ital">who does not purpose it from the night.</hi> (TA.                   <hi rend="ital">He decided upon the purpose,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">intention, by night,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in night-time.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">بَيَّتَ رَأْيَهُ</foreign>

                  <hi rend="ital">of hair</hi> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">hair-cloth</hi>] <hi rend="ital">is that kind</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of tent</hi>] <hi rend="ital">which has more than one pole:</hi> the word is masc.: and applies to <hi rend="ital">small</hi> and <hi rend="ital">large:</hi> (M:) tents of goats' hair are peculiar to people of cold countries and of fertile regions, where the goats have abundant hair; for the goats of the Arabs of the desert have short hair, not long enough to be spun: (T in art. <foreign lang="ar">بنى</foreign>:) a <foreign lang="ar">خِبَآء</foreign> is a small <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> of wool or of hair: a <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">what is larger than a</hi>

[See 1, last sentence.]          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  A <foreign lang="ar">بَيْت</foreign> of poetry, (T, S, M, Msb,) or of the poet, (K,) is <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">A verse;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">what consists of certain known divisions</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">feet</hi>] <hi rend="ital">called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَجْزَآءُ التَّفْعِيلِ</foreign>; being termed <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> metaphorically, because of the conjoining of its component parts, one to another, in a particular manner, like as those of a tent are conjoined in its construction; (Msb;) because it consists of words collected together in a regular manner, and so resembles a tent, which is composed of a <foreign lang="ar">سَقْف</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كِفَآء</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِوَاق</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">عُمُد</foreign>: (T:) it is derived from the same word signifying a <foreign lang="ar">خِبَآء</foreign> [or tent], and applies to the small and the great, as the <foreign lang="ar">رَجَز</foreign> and the <foreign lang="ar">طَوِيل</foreign>; and is [said to be] thus called because it comprises words like as the tent comprises its inhabitants; wherefore its component parts are termed <foreign lang="ar">أَسْبَاب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَوْتَاد</foreign>, as being likened to the <foreign lang="ar">اسباب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">اوتاد</foreign> of tents: (M:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَاتٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بُيُوتٌ</foreign>, (M, A, Msb,) the latter mentioned by Sb and IJ, (M,) [but rare,] and [pl. pl.] <foreign lang="ar">أَبَايِيتُ</foreign>: (A:) Abu-l-Hasan says that if the <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> of poetry be likened to the <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> which is a tent or other kind of structure, there is no reason why it should not have the same pl. forms as the latter has. (L.) By the following words of a poet, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَبَيْتٍ عَلَى ظَهْرِ المَطِىِّ بَنَيْتُهُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بِأَسْمَرَ مَشْقُوقِ الخَيَاشِيمِ يَرْعُفُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Many a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">upon the back of the camel have I</hi> 
                  <pb n="281"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">constructed with a lawny thing slit in the nose</hi> and <hi rend="ital">bleeding</hi>], is meant, many a <foreign lang="ar">بيت</foreign> of poetry have I written with the reed-pen. (S.) [<foreign lang="ar">البَيْتَ</foreign>, written after a quotation of a part of a verse of poetry, means <foreign lang="ar">اِقْرَأِ البَيْتَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Read thou the verse.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">بَيْتُ القَصِيدَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The</hi> chief <hi rend="ital">verse of the poem</hi>] is a phrase employed when a person composes a poem in praise of any one from whom he would obtain some object of desire and want, being applied to <hi rend="ital">that verse of the poem in which the author's want is mentioned:</hi> and is a proverbial expression relating to that which is extraordinary and strange, and used in denoting the superiority of a part of a thing over the whole of it [regarded as a whole]: [hence,] one says, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ أَوَّلُ الجَرِيدَةِ وَبَيْتُ القَصِيدَةِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Such a one is the first of the detachment of horsemen, and the chief verse of the poem</hi>]. (Har p. 441.)    </entryFree>29:T5b6,<entryFree id="n3604" key="بِيتَةٌ" type="main">

(S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Cold,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cool,</hi> water, (M, K,) <hi rend="ital">that has become so from its having remained throughout a night:</hi> (M:) or water <hi rend="ital">that remains during the night beneath the sky:</hi> (Ham p. 553:) or water <hi rend="ital">that has been cooled in the leathern bag by night;</hi> and in like manner, milk; for [Az says,] I heard an Arab of the desert say, <foreign lang="ar">اِسْقِنِى مِنْ بَيُّوتِ السِّقَآءِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Give thou me to drink of the milk that has been milked at night and left in the skin so that it has become cold,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cool, by night.</hi> (T.)
